<userid>102740701992931420698</userid><username>Linda Bott<//username><Date>1595977364019< /Date><Rate>1< /Rate>< text>
I've been going to Valvoline for over 10 years, probably since I moved to my current house nearby which was in 2004. But I will not be going back again. They are polite and I've no complaint about the oil change itself. There have been a few times in the past where I've felt they are really pushing for you to do something extra on your car, like change the cabin filter or get transmission service, but that's usually not too bad at all.

But for years, I have driven my car up, they check all the lights, and then I ask to wait outside of the car because I'm super sensitive to motion sickness. I get sea sick just walking on the dock before you even get on the boat, I get carsick, I feel queasy when an elevator first starts moving. It's only getting worse as I get older. When I told the worker that I always wait outside, he said because of the Covid pandemic, they can't have people leave their cars. I said I could just wait outside until they are done. He went to get the manager, who said if I were to wait outside, it will take a lot longer for the oil change. I told him that I was very sensitive to motion sickness and that it made me feel queasy when the car rocked a little during the oil change. He said the problem was that if I wait outside, they will have to keep coming over to talk to me during the oil change and that's why it will take longer. I told him that I did not want to buy any other services besides the oil change so they didn't need to ask me about them. He then said the car does not move during the oil change and he questioned whether I had ever sat in the car during one. I said that I had and it made me feel queasy and that is why I don't like to sit inside anymore. So he said that the car wouldn't move and that I had to stay inside and asked if I wanted them to work on my car or not. I feel like if I had made a scene and argued with him and gotten pushy, I might have been able to stay outside during the oil change, but I don't like to act like that. So I stayed in the car and had the oil change, but I did feel nauseous.

I don't want to give my business to a company that doesn't care about their customer's feelings. I asked politely about 3 times and that should be enough. I shouldn't have to argue or make a scene. There was no reason that I could not have waited outside of the car. Even though the Covid pandemic was going on, we were all wearing masks and I could have easily stepped out of the car and back inside when they were done without getting within 6 feet of any employees. Next time, I will try Jiffy Lube even though they are more expensive. Or I can always go to Goodyear or Firestone or one of the many other auto service choices available.</text>

< review>
Why go to a farmers' market, when you can go to the farm itself? Of course, you have to be in the area to visit. I've shopped with them at the Hollywood Farmers Market before, so I was familiar with their operation.
My friend and I were there just prior to Halloween, so they'd also setup a family friendly pumpkin patch along with wheel barrows to lug the pumpkins around!
In their store, there was a wide array of freshly picked produce. I was frankly impressed!<//review>

<Rate>2< /Rate>< review>
The good part of Rocklin Smiles is the pleasant and friendly atmosphere inside the building. Everyone is going out of their way to make you feel comfortable. The two stars however are an evaluation prompted by the actual work and its consequences. I went in just for a checkup with no pain or issues.  Dr Maasri stated that she detected a cavity and that the best solution would be a crown. We proceeded with the procedure but I was somewhat uneasy by the process; most of the actual crown work was done by an assistant (technician) and the post bite adjustment took maybe 5 minutes.  Dr. Maasri told me that I could come back for any issue. The pain over the next days was pretty substantial and grew to chronic pain into my lower and upper jaw reaching my cheekbone. When I started waking up at nights, I made a new appointment. During the second appointment new adjustment to my bite were done but again pain drove me to take ibuprofen for pain reduction and possible inflammation. After my third visit the bite was finally corrected as it should be and now I am pain free.
Again, the office is trying to be super friendly but the actual dentist work seems to be rushed in completion. My days and nights of pain could have been prevented by an extra 15-30 minutes of bite correction; it seems the dentist did not have the needed experience to identify and complete the bite correction properly.< /review>

< Review>
In my experience, Aldi has been great for grocery shopping. The prices for their items are very low, and the employees working there have always been helpful and friendly. The only possible downside is that their selection is much more limited than larger grocers, so they may not have everything you are looking for. If they have the items you need though, I would definitely head here first. They carry a lot of their own brand items, or items they partner with, and I am surprised at how often I prefer their brand over the commercial products. Usually this is not the case for me. These days I will only visit other grocers for the few things I can't find here.<//Review>

<user_name>Chris J<//user_name><text>GREAT PRICES! The place ain't big nor fancy and you bag yer own, but it is super clean, well lit and has very nice staff!  After purchase, there's a dedicated table/ shelf place for you to bag-up your groceries....which is nice if you bag kinda slowly...and it keeps  the checkout line moving fast.  If you don't care about brand names, Aldi's is the for you! Their generics are equal OR even better than the big name-brand products...for reals.  They have fancy stuff too, but it still costs less than all the other grocery stores in town.   They cut costs by not carrying multiple brand-names of the same item, but they do have all the basics.  Some specialty items too and their organic &vegetarian offerings are at CRAZY-LOW prices.  Don't forget to bring a quarter for the shopping cart (it's a quarter, big deal, and u get it back when u return the cart). They pass the savings to you by not having to pay someone else to collect carts from the parking lot all day.....so itz really WORTH the 2 minutes of my time to put the cart back.  They have weekly special items at shockingly low costs...just peruse their online ad and youll see.  You can't go wrong.   After shopping at Aldis and comparing, I honestly could NOT give five stars to any other grocery store in Lancaster.  FIVE STARS FOR ALDI!</text><Resp>None< /Resp>< GmapID>
